## Isaiah 44:6–20 (id: 16376)

This passage uses the form of a trial speech to press God’s argument that disgrace comes to all who trust in idols and false gods.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:6–ISA 44:20

## Isaiah 44:15–17 (id: 16367)

he uses part of the wood to make a fire . . . he takes the rest of it and makes himself a god to worship: This description of the process of making an idol drips with sarcasm and ridicule at the stupidity of the foolish idol worshipers (see also [44:19](https://ref.ly/Isa44:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:15–ISA 44:17

## Isaiah 44:18–19 (id: 16368)

Their minds are shut: Idol worshipers cannot see the irony in using one part of a log to warm themselves and another part of the same log to be their god.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:18–ISA 44:19

## Isaiah 44:21–22 (id: 16369)

The Lord promised to forgive Israel’s sins.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:21–ISA 44:22

## Isaiah 44:23 (id: 16370)

All creation is called to celebrate God’s redemption of Israel (cp. [1:2](https://ref.ly/Isa1:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:23

## Isaiah 44:24–45.8 (id: 16371)

The Lord alone is sovereign over history. He raised up Cyrus of Persia to execute judgment on Babylon and restore Israel to the Holy Land.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:24–ISA 45:8

## Isaiah 44:25 (id: 16372)

False prophets and fortune\-tellers used forbidden forms of divination to try to predict the future. Eventually God would expose them as deluded liars (see [3:2](https://ref.ly/Isa3:2); [9:15](https://ref.ly/Isa9:15); [47:13](https://ref.ly/Isa47:13); [Deut 18:10–11](https://ref.ly/Deut18:10-Deut18:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:25

## Isaiah 44:27 (id: 16373)

The sudden depletion of natural resources at times indicates a divine judgment (see [42:15](https://ref.ly/Isa42:15); cp. [43:20](https://ref.ly/Isa43:20)). Here, however, God’s ability to dry up streams with just a word illustrates his power to do what he said he would do through Cyrus of Persia.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:27

## Isaiah 44:28 (id: 16374)

He is my shepherd: Cyrus went beyond simply permitting the Jews to return to their homeland. He facilitated a major restoration project to rebuild Jerusalem and restore the Temple (see [45:13](https://ref.ly/Isa45:13); [Ezra 1:2–4](https://ref.ly/Ezra1:2-Ezra1:4); [6:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ezra6:3-Ezra6:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 44:28

## Isaiah 45:1 (id: 16381)

anointed one: This designation, commonly reserved for David or the Messiah, is here applied to Cyrus. Cyrus was anointed in the sense that he was selected to fulfill a special mission. This title was never used of any other foreign ruler (cp. [1 Sam 10:1](https://ref.ly/1Sam10:1); [Rom 13:1](https://ref.ly/Rom13:1)). • whose right hand he will empower: The Lord would give Cyrus victory over Babylon (see [Isa 43:14](https://ref.ly/Isa43:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:1

## Isaiah 45:3 (id: 16386)

so you may know: Cyrus’s victories provided factual proof that the Lord has the power to fulfill his plans, whereas idols and false gods do not (see [41:21–29](https://ref.ly/Isa41:21-Isa41:29)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:3

## Isaiah 45:4–5 (id: 16387)

I call you by name: Cyrus did not know the Lord, but the Lord knew him. Isaiah predicted the rescuer Cyrus by name 150 years in advance. This prophecy would prove to the exiles that the Lord is indeed God and that he knows the future.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:4–ISA 45:5

## Isaiah 45:7 (id: 16388)

light . . . darkness . . . good times and bad times: Everything is under God’s control.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:7

## Isaiah 45:9–11 (id: 16389)

pot . . . its maker . . . baby . . . its father: It is ridiculous for a creature to question the wisdom of its creator.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:9–ISA 45:11

## Isaiah 45:9–13 (id: 16390)

The Lord confronts those who question his right to use a pagan king to achieve his purposes. He, the Creator, is free and sovereign in his activities. He promised to bring his people back to their land, and he would use anyone he chose to accomplish that purpose.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:9–ISA 45:13

## Isaiah 45:14 (id: 16377)

Egyptians . . . Ethiopians . . . Sabeans: Israel’s restoration would bring them a new sovereignty. Foreign nations would honor God, and because they recognized God’s special blessing on his people, they would also want to honor his people.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:14

## Isaiah 45:17 (id: 16378)

Israel would never again be humiliated and disgraced*,* oppressed, harassed, or abused. The finality of these declarations suggests that this promise will be fulfilled at the end of time.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:17

## Isaiah 45:18 (id: 16380)

Ancient pagan people viewed the world as a place of empty chaos. However, God’s purposes are good, and he made the world from the beginning as a place to be lived in with him in harmony.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:18

## Isaiah 45:18–25 (id: 16379)

Salvation is from the Lord alone. He is the creator, the revealer, and the executor of his will in human history. He promised to establish a new era of salvation and righteousness (see [45:8](https://ref.ly/Isa45:8)). Every human being will submit to God, either willingly or unwillingly ([45:23–24](https://ref.ly/Isa45:23-Isa45:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:18–ISA 45:25

## Isaiah 45:22 (id: 16382)

Let all the world look to me: All humanity needs to seek the Lord, the true God who created all things, while he may be found ([55:6](https://ref.ly/Isa55:6)). • In God there is salvation*,* the only hope for all of humanity ([45:8](https://ref.ly/Isa45:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:22

## Isaiah 45:23 (id: 16383)

God’s words are always true. God’s swearing by his own name reinforces the certainty that he will never go back on his word (see also [14:24](https://ref.ly/Isa14:24); [54:9](https://ref.ly/Isa54:9); [62:8](https://ref.ly/Isa62:8); [Heb 6:13](https://ref.ly/Heb6:13)). • Every knee . . . every tongue: At the end of time all nations will submit to his authority, whether willingly or unwillingly (see [Rom 14:11](https://ref.ly/Rom14:11); [1 Cor 15:25–27](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:25-1Cor15:27); [Phil 2:10–11](https://ref.ly/Phil2:10-Phil2:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:23

## Isaiah 45:24 (id: 16384)

In this context, the people are all who turn to the Lord for salvation, even those from foreign nations ([45:22](https://ref.ly/Isa45:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:24

## Isaiah 45:25 (id: 16385)

justified: Literally *righteous* (see also [45:8](https://ref.ly/Isa45:8), [24](https://ref.ly/Isa45:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 45:25

## Isaiah 46:1 (id: 16396)

*Marduk\-bel* was the most important god in the Babylonian pantheon. Bel (similar to “Baal”) designated lordship. • Nebo (*Nabu,* *Nebu*), the patron deity of Babylonian scribes, was thought to be the son of Marduk\-bel. • Instead of being paraded in glory at a Babylonian festival, these gods would be hauled away on ox carts and disposed of, rejected by the Babylonian people.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:1

## Isaiah 46:1–2 (id: 16391)

This taunt was against the self\-contradiction of Babylonian religion.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:1–ISA 46:2

## Isaiah 46:3 (id: 16397)

Those who remain in Israel refers to the remnant that would be left alive after the destruction of Jerusalem in 586 BC. • The Lord, the Creator of humanity, cares for and carries his people (contrast the Babylonian idols that must be carried instead). • since you were born . . . before you were born: The Lord chose Israel even before they were a nation (see also [49:5](https://ref.ly/Isa49:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:3

## Isaiah 46:8–13 (id: 16398)

Many of the exiles would be completely discouraged and not believe the prediction of God’s rescue. God challenged this unbelief.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:8–ISA 46:13

## Isaiah 46:10 (id: 16392)

God knows the future before it even happens*;* he has comprehensive control over all events, and all his acts match his words ([41:4](https://ref.ly/Isa41:4), [26](https://ref.ly/Isa41:26)). He is the First and the Last ([44:6](https://ref.ly/Isa44:6); [48:12](https://ref.ly/Isa48:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:10

## Isaiah 46:11 (id: 16393)

The swift bird of prey from the east refers to Cyrus, the Persian king (see study note on 41:2).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:11
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 41:2 (ID: `16332@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 46:12 (id: 16394)

Formerly, Israel cared little for doing right (literally *righteousness;* see also [58:2](https://ref.ly/Isa58:2); [59:9](https://ref.ly/Isa59:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:12

## Isaiah 46:13 (id: 16395)

The good news for Israel was that God was coming to set things right (literally *I will bring my righteousness near;* see [40:9](https://ref.ly/Isa40:9); [51:5](https://ref.ly/Isa51:5)). • show my glory to Israel: Unlike a craftsman who bestows material splendor on an idol ([44:13](https://ref.ly/Isa44:13)), the Lord bestows true dignity on his people.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 46:13

## Isaiah 47:1 (id: 16404)

To sit in the dust was a way of expressing humiliation.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:1

## Isaiah 47:1–4 (id: 16400)

In this taunt against Babylon, the queen of nations is humiliated, forced to work as a servant girl.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:1–ISA 47:4

## Isaiah 47:1–48.22 (id: 16399)

Two conclusions can be drawn from the preceding evidence that the Lord alone is God: (1\) Babylon’s great pride is foolishness ([47:1–15](https://ref.ly/Isa47:1-Isa47:15)); (2\) Israel needs to pay attention to the word of the Lord ([48:1–22](https://ref.ly/Isa48:1-Isa48:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:1–ISA 48:22

## Isaiah 47:3 (id: 16405)

God’s vengeance against those who oppose him and those who oppress his people (see [34:8](https://ref.ly/Isa34:8)) will bring justice to the world by purging it of wickedness.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:3

## Isaiah 47:5–11 (id: 16406)

Babylon’s confidence and arrogance were well known (see [14:13–17](https://ref.ly/Isa14:13-Isa14:17); [Dan 4:30](https://ref.ly/Dan4:30)). All of this nation’s charms, magic, and wisdom were useless against the disaster decreed for it.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:5–ISA 47:11

## Isaiah 47:6 (id: 16407)

The people of Israel had provoked God’s wrath, prompting him to use Babylon to punish them. Now wicked Babylon itself would be punished.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:6

## Isaiah 47:8 (id: 16408)

I am the only one, and there is no other: This was a claim to divinity (cp. [45:5](https://ref.ly/Isa45:5); [47:10](https://ref.ly/Isa47:10)). Only the Lord can make such a claim. For any created thing, including a nation, to utter this is the height of hubris. • To be a widow or to lose one’s children was a disgrace.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:8

## Isaiah 47:9 (id: 16409)

Witchcraft and magic were commonly used in an attempt to ward off evil and to secure a happy future.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:9

## Isaiah 47:10 (id: 16401)

In this context, ‘wisdom’ and ‘knowledge’ probably refer sarcastically to the pseudo\-knowledge gained through occult practices, which actually led Babylon away from the truth and into disaster ([47:11](https://ref.ly/Isa47:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:10

## Isaiah 47:12–15 (id: 16402)

In the face of calamity, Babylon would turn to occult practices for help, but it would not find help.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:12–ISA 47:15

## Isaiah 47:13 (id: 16403)

Babylon was advanced in astronomy, which the astrologers and stargazers used as a form of divination (see [Dan 2:2](https://ref.ly/Dan2:2), [10](https://ref.ly/Dan2:10); [5:7](https://ref.ly/Dan5:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 47:13

## Isaiah 48:1 (id: 16421)

Jacob . . . Judah: Although Isaiah’s normal focus was on Judah, here he addressed all the tribes of Israel.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:1

## Isaiah 48:1–2 (id: 16412)

Israel was religious but not truly committed to the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:1–ISA 48:2

## Isaiah 48:1–11 (id: 16410)

This prophecy is a *disputation,* a speech in which the prophet argues a set of points against his audience.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:1–ISA 48:11

## Isaiah 48:1–22 (id: 16411)

The Lord here calls on Israel to forsake her historic rebelliousness and listen to what he says. The Hebrew word translated *listening* is often synonymous with *obeying* or acting upon what is heard.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:1–ISA 48:22

## Isaiah 48:3 (id: 16425)

The Lord had forewarned Israel of what was going to happen in the Exile.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:3

## Isaiah 48:6–7 (id: 16426)

Even though Israel had repeatedly failed to believe God’s past predictions, here he revealed new things that were not yet heard. Specifically, God revealed that Babylon would fall and Israel would be restored.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:6–ISA 48:7

## Isaiah 48:10 (id: 16413)

The Exile was a furnace of suffering (cp. [Deut 4:20](https://ref.ly/Deut4:20)) through which God refined Israel.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:10

## Isaiah 48:11 (id: 16414)

I will not let my reputation be tarnished: Israel’s exile raised questions among the nations about the Lord’s character and reputation. The nations would not have perceived that Israel’s wicked character led to the Exile. Instead they would have viewed it as a failure of Israel’s God to protect his people and their land (see [36:19–20](https://ref.ly/Isa36:19-Isa36:20); [37:12](https://ref.ly/Isa37:12); [Ezek 36:19–26](https://ref.ly/Ezek36:19-Ezek36:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:11

## Isaiah 48:12–22 (id: 16415)

This final trial speech reviews the arguments of chs [40–48](https://ref.ly/Isa40:1-Isa48:22) and announces the final conclusion.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:12–ISA 48:22

## Isaiah 48:14 (id: 16416)

chosen Cyrus (literally *him*) as his ally: See [44:28](https://ref.ly/Isa44:28); [45:1–2](https://ref.ly/Isa45:1-Isa45:2).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:14

## Isaiah 48:15 (id: 16417)

I will send him and will help him succeed: Cyrus would humiliate Babylon and liberate Israel ([45:1–4](https://ref.ly/Isa45:1-Isa45:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:15

## Isaiah 48:16 (id: 16418)

I have told you plainly: God’s promises are clear, though not always specific as to manner and time. • now the Sovereign Lord and his Spirit have sent me with this message: The identity of the one who is sent is unclear. Isaiah might be referring to himself as a Spirit\-inspired prophet who spoke the very words of God to Israel. The connection with the Spirit suggests that it refers to the promised servant, the Messiah. • The presence of the Spirit assures the servant’s success.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:16

## Isaiah 48:18 (id: 16419)

Peace and righteousness will be established when the Kingdom of God comes in its fullness (see [66:12](https://ref.ly/Isa66:12)). • like a gentle river . . . like waves: An abundance of comforting peace and overflowing resources of righteousness (cp. [Amos 5:24](https://ref.ly/Amos5:24)) could have been Israel’s if its people had only listened to God.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:18

## Isaiah 48:19 (id: 16420)

Your descendants . . . like the sands: This would fulfill God’s covenant to Abraham ([Gen 22:17](https://ref.ly/Gen22:17)); by contrast, the Israelites were nearly wiped out in the Exile (see [Isa 44:26](https://ref.ly/Isa44:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:19

## Isaiah 48:20 (id: 16422)

Leave Babylon: See also [52:11–12](https://ref.ly/Isa52:11-Isa52:12); [55:12](https://ref.ly/Isa55:12).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:20

## Isaiah 48:21 (id: 16423)

not thirsty . . . rock . . . water gushed: These reminders of God’s provision in the Exodus provide a fitting summary of what he would do to rescue Israel from captivity in Babylon (see [Num 20:11](https://ref.ly/Num20:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:21

## Isaiah 48:22 (id: 16424)

This refrain, no peace for the wicked (also [57:21](https://ref.ly/Isa57:21)), continues the sharp divide between the godly and the wicked (see [66:24](https://ref.ly/Isa66:24)). Peace speaks of God’s kingdom, from which the wicked are excluded.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 48:22

## Isaiah 49:1 (id: 16435)

distant lands: The servant’s ministry would extend beyond Israel (see [42:4](https://ref.ly/Isa42:4), [10](https://ref.ly/Isa42:10), [12](https://ref.ly/Isa42:12); [51:5](https://ref.ly/Isa51:5); [60:9](https://ref.ly/Isa60:9); [66:19](https://ref.ly/Isa66:19)). • called me before my birth . . . from within the womb . . . by name: The promised servant’s prophetic call was similar to the call of Jeremiah (see [Jer 1:5](https://ref.ly/Jer1:5); see also [Gal 1:15](https://ref.ly/Gal1:15)). It was not a general call but a very specific, personal one (see also [Isa 43:1](https://ref.ly/Isa43:1); [45:3–4](https://ref.ly/Isa45:3-Isa45:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:1

## Isaiah 49:1–13 (id: 16427)

This has traditionally been regarded as the second of four suffering servant songs (see study note on 42:1–4). The suffering role of the promised servant becomes increasingly clear (see also [50:4–9](https://ref.ly/Isa50:4-Isa50:9); [52:13–53:12](https://ref.ly/Isa52:13-Isa53:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:1–ISA 49:13
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 42:1-4 (ID: `16339@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 49:1–55.13 (id: 16428)

God intended to rescue the Israelites from exile. However, the question remained: How could sinful Israel again become the servant of the Holy One? God would make a way for Israel’s sin to be atoned for and their fellowship with him to be restored. That way would be the promised servant, who would come for Israel and for all peoples. This servant was introduced in [42:1–9](https://ref.ly/Isa42:1-Isa42:9), but in this passage he becomes the central focus.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:1–ISA 49:7

## Isaiah 49:2 (id: 16440)

my words of judgment: The servant’s mission would be prophetic (see [11:4](https://ref.ly/Isa11:4); [Eph 6:17](https://ref.ly/Eph6:17); [Heb 4:12](https://ref.ly/Heb4:12); [Rev 1:16](https://ref.ly/Rev1:16); [2:12](https://ref.ly/Rev2:12), [16](https://ref.ly/Rev2:16); [19:15](https://ref.ly/Rev19:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:2

## Isaiah 49:3 (id: 16441)

The suffering servant would come out of Israel (see [41:8](https://ref.ly/Isa41:8)) and would himself be the true Israel. He would serve as both king ([42:1](https://ref.ly/Isa42:1)) and prophet ([49:1](https://ref.ly/Isa49:1)), anointed with the Spirit of God ([61:1](https://ref.ly/Isa61:1)) and commissioned ([48:16](https://ref.ly/Isa48:16)) as a faithful witness to God’s purposes ([43:12](https://ref.ly/Isa43:12); [48:20](https://ref.ly/Isa48:20)). In his mission toward both Israel and the other nations ([49:6](https://ref.ly/Isa49:6)), he would suffer rejection and disgrace while being faithful, unlike the nation of Israel (see [50:4–9](https://ref.ly/Isa50:4-Isa50:9)). His suffering would be on behalf of God’s chosen people. Jesus became the ultimate fulfillment of the suffering servant (see study note on 52:13–53:12).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:3
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 52:13-53.12 (ID: `16507@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 49:4 (id: 16442)

my work seems so useless . . . to no purpose: Even though people stubbornly refuse his message, the servant would reach out to them. • I will trust God: Despite discouragement and suffering, the servant would continue to discharge his duty faithfully, trusting God for the outcome. God promised to reward the servant’s faithfulness (see also [40:10](https://ref.ly/Isa40:10); [50:8](https://ref.ly/Isa50:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:4

## Isaiah 49:6 (id: 16443)

a light to the Gentiles: As the Messiah, the servant’s mission would have a worldwide reach (see [11:10](https://ref.ly/Isa11:10), [12](https://ref.ly/Isa11:12); [42:6](https://ref.ly/Isa42:6)). The apostle Paul explained his apostolic mission to the Gentiles on the basis of this prophecy ([Acts 13:47](https://ref.ly/Acts13:47); [26:23](https://ref.ly/Acts26:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:6

## Isaiah 49:7 (id: 16444)

The promised servant would be despised and rejected by the nations (see [52:14–53:5](https://ref.ly/Isa52:14-Isa53:5)) as well as by his own people (see also [50:6–7](https://ref.ly/Isa50:6-Isa50:7); [53:8–9](https://ref.ly/Isa53:8-Isa53:9)). • Kings and princes will also bow low to express respect and humility before the servant (see also [52:15](https://ref.ly/Isa52:15)), whom God will exalt after he has suffered. God is faithful to his servant.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:7

## Isaiah 49:8 (id: 16445)

God acts at just the right time to accomplish his purposes ([Acts 1:7](https://ref.ly/Acts1:7); [2 Cor 6:2](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:2)). Israel returned to reestablish the land of Israel after the Exile. The land was restored and the city rebuilt beginning with Cyrus’s edict ([Isa 44:26–28](https://ref.ly/Isa44:26-Isa44:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:8

## Isaiah 49:10–11 (id: 16429)

Like a shepherd, the Lord in his mercy will lead the returning exiles beside cool waters*;* he promised to comfort them and tend to their needs (see also [40:11](https://ref.ly/Isa40:11); [Ps 23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1)). • level paths . . . highways: The Lord would open up the way of salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:10–ISA 49:11

## Isaiah 49:12 (id: 16430)

The remnant would come from the north (i.e., from Babylon and Persia), from the west by sea, and from as far south as Egypt.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:12

## Isaiah 49:13 (id: 16431)

This hymn of praise is in response to the salvation that the servant would make possible.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:13

## Isaiah 49:14 (id: 16432)

Although the prophet announced cause for rejoicing ([49:8–13](https://ref.ly/Isa49:8-Isa49:13)), the exiles continued to ponder the calamity that came upon them when Babylon invaded the land, destroyed Jerusalem*,* and carried the people of Judah into exile where they felt deserted and forgotten.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:14

## Isaiah 49:18 (id: 16433)

like jewels or bridal ornaments: As a wedding calls for festivity and public display, so God’s restoration of Israel would be an open act for all to see (see also [61:10](https://ref.ly/Isa61:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:18

## Isaiah 49:19–21 (id: 16434)

The population explosion would reach beyond Israel to include the members of foreign nations who turn to the Lord (see [56:6–8](https://ref.ly/Isa56:6-Isa56:8); [Rev 7:9](https://ref.ly/Rev7:9)). • more room: The expanded population would require space far beyond the traditional boundaries of the land of Israel (see also [Zech 2:4](https://ref.ly/Zech2:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:19–ISA 49:21

## Isaiah 49:22 (id: 16436)

carry your little sons . . . your daughters: The mighty rulers of the nations, some of whom had previously killed children in Israel, would aid in their return to Zion (see also [60:3–9](https://ref.ly/Isa60:3-Isa60:9)). Elsewhere Isaiah envisioned people of foreign nations streaming to Zion to worship the Lord (see [2:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2-Isa2:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:22

## Isaiah 49:23 (id: 16437)

you will know that I am the Lord: The stunning role\-reversal—kings and queens serving the lowly exiles upon their return—would reveal God’s power to do the unimaginable (see also [60:16](https://ref.ly/Isa60:16)). • The godly would experience temporary disgrace in the Exile but would not ultimately be put to shame*,* as the idolaters and ungodly were.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:23

## Isaiah 49:24 (id: 16438)

Who can snatch . . . Who can demand: The people considered it nearly impossible that they would be rescued from their oppressors.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:24

## Isaiah 49:25 (id: 16439)

The Lord is like a warrior who will fight to protect his children, as promised to Abraham ([Gen 12:3](https://ref.ly/Gen12:3); see also [Isa 54:15](https://ref.ly/Isa54:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 49:25

## Isaiah 50:1 (id: 16476)

God was not at fault for the people’s problems; it was their sin that brought about their exile (see also [59:1–15](https://ref.ly/Isa59:1-Isa59:15)). • Jerusalem—the mother city of Judah ([Ps 87:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps87:5-Ps87:6))—was destroyed, and the people of Judah were taken into exile in 586 BC.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:1

## Isaiah 50:1–3 (id: 16472)

This disputation shows that God was not forced to give Israel up, and therefore he could take the nation back as his people if he desired.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:1–ISA 50:3

## Isaiah 50:2 (id: 16477)

Why didn’t anyone answer: The people had not responded to God’s repeated call to trust in him and repent of their sins. They were deaf and stubborn (see [6:9–10](https://ref.ly/Isa6:9-Isa6:10); [29:18](https://ref.ly/Isa29:18); [35:5](https://ref.ly/Isa35:5); [42:18–19](https://ref.ly/Isa42:18-Isa42:19)). • The Lord came and called the people through the prophets (see also [65:1–3](https://ref.ly/Isa65:1-Isa65:3)). • Is it because I have no power to rescue? God was fully able to rescue Israel and Judah from the Assyrians and Babylonians, but he first had to deal justly with his people’s sinfulness (see [59:1](https://ref.ly/Isa59:1)). • speak to the sea and make it dry: This was an allusion to the parting of the Red Sea during the exodus from Egypt ([Exod 14:21–22](https://ref.ly/Exod14:21-Exod14:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:2

## Isaiah 50:3 (id: 16478)

Phenomena such as darkness and the wearing of clothes of mourning were associated with the day of the Lord ([13:10](https://ref.ly/Isa13:10); see study note on 2:5–22). The mention of darkness might allude to the plague of darkness in Egypt ([Exod 10:21](https://ref.ly/Exod10:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:3
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 2:5-22 (ID: `15969@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 50:4 (id: 16480)

The Lord, who never grows weary ([40:28](https://ref.ly/Isa40:28)), sends the servant with good news (see [40:28–31](https://ref.ly/Isa40:28-Isa40:31)) to comfort those who are weary (see study note on 40:1–31).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:4
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 40:1-31 (ID: `16290@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 50:4–11 (id: 16479)

This is the third of four servant songs (see study note on 42:1–4). The faithful and suffering servant portrays an ideal Israel; the image was realized in Jesus Christ.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:4–ISA 50:11
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 42:1-4 (ID: `16339@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 50:6 (id: 16481)

beat me . . . pulled out my beard . . . mockery and spitting: These connections with the experience of Jesus at his crucifixion are too close to be coincidental—Jesus is the true suffering servant (see [Matt 27:27–31](https://ref.ly/Matt27:27-Matt27:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:6

## Isaiah 50:7 (id: 16482)

Externally, the servant would be disgraced and put to shame*,* but within himself he would calmly await God’s vindication (see [29:22](https://ref.ly/Isa29:22); [54:4](https://ref.ly/Isa54:4); [61:7](https://ref.ly/Isa61:7)). • set my face like a stone: The servant would be determined to do God’s will (see [Luke 9:51](https://ref.ly/Luke9:51)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:7

## Isaiah 50:8 (id: 16483)

He who gives me justice is near: God vindicates those who suffer for doing his will. Vindication is an act of God by which he exalts those who have been wrongly disgraced and strikes down the wicked, self\-exalted, and arrogant (see also [2 Thes 1:6–9](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:6-2Thess1:9)). • bring charges . . . my accusers: Confidence in God’s vindication removes fear and bolsters faith (see [Rom 8:31–34](https://ref.ly/Rom8:31-Rom8:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:8

## Isaiah 50:9 (id: 16484)

Who will declare me guilty? The implied answer to this rhetorical question is, “No one!” This answer foreshadows the New Testament understanding of justification (see [Rom 8:31–35](https://ref.ly/Rom8:31-Rom8:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:9

## Isaiah 50:10 (id: 16474)

The test of whether or not an individual fears the Lord is how he or she responds to God’s righteous servant. The same idea is present in Jesus’ claim that no one can come to the Father except through him ([John 14:6](https://ref.ly/John14:6)). • Those who trust in the Lord have great hope for the future (see [Isa 12:2](https://ref.ly/Isa12:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:10

## Isaiah 50:10–11 (id: 16473)

This is a call for response to the servant’s ministry.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:10–ISA 50:11

## Isaiah 50:11 (id: 16475)

warm yourselves by your own fires: Spiritually complacent people are unresponsive toward God. Though they have comfort and security now, they will soon fall down in great torment (see [66:24](https://ref.ly/Isa66:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 50:11

## Isaiah 51:1 (id: 16492)

The rock and the quarry represent Abraham and Sarah ([51:2](https://ref.ly/Isa51:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:1

## Isaiah 51:1–8 (id: 16485)

This prophecy calls for trust in the Lord. Each of its three units begins with the phrase, Listen to me ([51:1](https://ref.ly/Isa51:1), [4](https://ref.ly/Isa51:4), [7](https://ref.ly/Isa51:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:1–ISA 51:8

## Isaiah 51:2 (id: 16496)

Abraham . . . became a great nation: The exiled community had decreased in number. They needed to have faith that God could restore them again to a healthy and thriving population.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:2

## Isaiah 51:3 (id: 16497)

Eden . . . the garden of the Lord: God’s salvation will one day reestablish conditions like those in which human beings first lived (see [Gen 2–3](https://ref.ly/Gen2:1-Gen3:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:3

## Isaiah 51:4 (id: 16498)

my law . . . my justice: The work of the servant will prosper because justice will be the rule in God’s kingdom on earth (see [42:1–4](https://ref.ly/Isa42:1-Isa42:4)). • a light to the nations: The nations will receive the Lord and his revelation (see also [42:6](https://ref.ly/Isa42:6); [49:6](https://ref.ly/Isa49:6); [60:1–3](https://ref.ly/Isa60:1-Isa60:3); [66:19–23](https://ref.ly/Isa66:19-Isa66:23); [Matt 4:15–16](https://ref.ly/Matt4:15-Matt4:16); [Luke 2:32](https://ref.ly/Luke2:32); [John 1:4–9](https://ref.ly/John1:4-John1:9); [12:35–50](https://ref.ly/John12:35-John12:50); [Acts 13:47](https://ref.ly/Acts13:47)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:4

## Isaiah 51:5 (id: 16499)

God is strong enough to crush his enemies and rescue his people, such as when he rescued Israel in the Exodus (see [51:9](https://ref.ly/Isa51:9); [Exod 6:6](https://ref.ly/Exod6:6); [15:16](https://ref.ly/Exod15:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:5

## Isaiah 51:6 (id: 16500)

die like flies: The wicked will die in great multitudes on the day of God’s judgment.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:6

## Isaiah 51:7 (id: 16501)

cherish my law in your hearts: Beyond simply knowing God’s word, the Lord desires for his people to internalize, treasure, and obey it (see also [Ps 37:31](https://ref.ly/Ps37:31); [Jer 31:33](https://ref.ly/Jer31:33)). • Those who obey the Lord often endure scorn and insults (see also [Matt 5:10–12](https://ref.ly/Matt5:10-Matt5:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:7

## Isaiah 51:9–10 (id: 16502)

Wake up, wake up: God does not sleep; this prayer is for God to act immediately to save his people (see [52:1](https://ref.ly/Isa52:1); see especially God’s military garb in [59:17](https://ref.ly/Isa59:17)). • in the days of old: The exodus from Egypt was an act of redemption that displayed God’s power as he made a path of escape ([51:10](https://ref.ly/Isa51:10)) for his people (see also [11:15](https://ref.ly/Isa11:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:9–ISA 51:10

## Isaiah 51:13 (id: 16486)

you have forgotten the Lord: The Lord will never forget Israel (see [44:21](https://ref.ly/Isa44:21); [49:15](https://ref.ly/Isa49:15)), so they should not forget him. • The Creator of the world also created the nation Israel.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:13

## Isaiah 51:14 (id: 16487)

The Exile brought such brutal conditions as imprisonment, starvation, and death.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:14

## Isaiah 51:15 (id: 16488)

I am the Lord: The Lord uses this formula to identify himself as the covenant God and to assure his people of the truth of his word and the reliability of his actions (see [27:3–4](https://ref.ly/Isa27:3-Isa27:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:15

## Isaiah 51:16 (id: 16489)

my words in your mouth: The focus shifted back to the servant. • You are my people: Israel was the covenant community.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:16

## Isaiah 51:17 (id: 16491)

Wake up, wake up: Israel used these words in a prayer to the Lord ([51:9](https://ref.ly/Isa51:9)). Israel’s problems were not the result of God’s slowness to act; rather, the people were slow to believe God’s promises. • the cup of the Lord’s fury: The Lord will appropriately measure out his judgment; those who fall under his judgment must figuratively drink from his wrath (see also [Matt 26:39](https://ref.ly/Matt26:39)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:17

## Isaiah 51:17–23 (id: 16490)

The prophet called the people of Israel to be done with their past and to anticipate God’s future for them.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:17–ISA 51:23

## Isaiah 51:20 (id: 16493)

children have fainted: A sad commentary on Jerusalem’s desolation is provided in [Lamentations 1:13](https://ref.ly/Lam1:13), [22](https://ref.ly/Lam1:22); [2:11–12](https://ref.ly/Lam2:11-Lam2:12), [19](https://ref.ly/Lam2:19).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:20

## Isaiah 51:22 (id: 16494)

God would be the Defender of Israel as he was when Assyria besieged Jerusalem ([38:6](https://ref.ly/Isa38:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:22

## Isaiah 51:23 (id: 16495)

The tormentors were the Babylonians who brought about destruction, war, and famine ([51:19](https://ref.ly/Isa51:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 51:23

## Isaiah 52:1 (id: 16512)

This second call to wake up (see [51:17](https://ref.ly/Isa51:17)) was in preparation for a glorious future. • holy city: The new city would be holy because its citizens would be holy (see [4:3](https://ref.ly/Isa4:3)). • enter your gates no longer: Things that are unclean will not be permitted to enter the holy city (see [Rev 21:27](https://ref.ly/Rev21:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:1

## Isaiah 52:3 (id: 16513)

I sold you into exile . . . Now I can redeem you: The Lord was fully in control when he gave his people into the hands of their enemies. Likewise, he remained fully in control and could redeem them if he chose to do so.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:3

## Isaiah 52:4 (id: 16514)

in Egypt . . . oppressed by Assyria: The exodus from exile would be like Israel’s past exodus from Egypt.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:4

## Isaiah 52:5 (id: 16515)

The oppressors would shout in exultation because they believed they had conquered not only Israel but also its God. • My name is blasphemed all day long: The condition of God’s people affects God’s reputation in the eyes of the watching world (see [37:6](https://ref.ly/Isa37:6), [23](https://ref.ly/Isa37:23); [48:11](https://ref.ly/Isa48:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:5

## Isaiah 52:6 (id: 16516)

Just as God did to Moses before the Exodus ([Exod 3:15](https://ref.ly/Exod3:15)), he will reveal himself in the coming rescue from exile.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:6

## Isaiah 52:7 (id: 16518)

How beautiful on the mountains: See [Nah 1:15](https://ref.ly/Nah1:15); [Rom 10:15](https://ref.ly/Rom10:15). • The good news goes beyond proclaiming an end to the Exile; it also points to the peace and salvation of the age to come ([Isa 54:13–14](https://ref.ly/Isa54:13-Isa54:14); see [40:9–10](https://ref.ly/Isa40:9-Isa40:10); [41:27](https://ref.ly/Isa41:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:7

## Isaiah 52:7–12 (id: 16517)

This is a poetic description of God’s promise to rescue his people from the alienation their sin created. The imagery is of a besieged city waiting for word that its hero has defeated the enemy armies. Paul applies these words to the proclamation of the Good News of the Lord Jesus ([Rom 10:15](https://ref.ly/Rom10:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:7–ISA 52:12

## Isaiah 52:8 (id: 16519)

The watchmen were those looking for the news of Zion’s redemption. • the Lord returning to Jerusalem: The sin of the city’s inhabitants had driven God away.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:8

## Isaiah 52:10 (id: 16503)

victory of our God: The rescue of God’s people from disgrace foreshadows an even greater victory when God will reign victoriously to the ends of the earth (note the many similarities with [Ps 98:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps98:1-Ps98:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:10

## Isaiah 52:11 (id: 16505)

Here the imagery of leaving the unclean enemy city encourages the people to purify themselves by turning away from all known sin. Those who carry home the sacred objects of the Lord need to be pure.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:11

## Isaiah 52:11–12 (id: 16504)

This is an exhortation to leave the captivity of sin (see [48:20](https://ref.ly/Isa48:20) on leaving physical captivity in Babylon). See also [2 Cor 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17); [2 Tim 2:19](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:19).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:11–ISA 52:12

## Isaiah 52:12 (id: 16506)

not leave in a hurry: At the time of the Exodus the people had to leave quickly (see [Exod 12:11](https://ref.ly/Exod12:11), [31–36](https://ref.ly/Exod12:31-Exod12:36)). Isaiah drew this contrast to emphasize the newness of God’s plan. • protect you from behind: See [Exod 13:21](https://ref.ly/Exod13:21); [14:19–20](https://ref.ly/Exod14:19-Exod14:20).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:12

## Isaiah 52:13 (id: 16508)

prosper . . . be highly exalted: The servant would be wise and successful, set apart with the great and noble. Similar terms describe God in [6:1](https://ref.ly/Isa6:1) and [57:15](https://ref.ly/Isa57:15).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:13

## Isaiah 52:13–53.12 (id: 16507)

This is the fourth of four passages that speak about the promised servant (see study note on 42:1–4). The Hebrew poem is carefully constructed in five three\-line stanzas. It begins with the servant’s exaltation ([52:13](https://ref.ly/Isa52:13)), proceeds to his humiliation ([52:14–53:9](https://ref.ly/Isa52:14-Isa53:9)), and ends with his exaltation ([53:10–12](https://ref.ly/Isa53:10-Isa53:12)). The faithful servant’s suffering would bring reconciliation between God and humans. The Lord Jesus perfectly fulfilled this prophecy (see ch [40](https://ref.ly/Isa40:1-Isa40:31); [Matt 8:17](https://ref.ly/Matt8:17); [Acts 8:30–35](https://ref.ly/Acts8:30-Acts8:35); [Rom 10:15–17](https://ref.ly/Rom10:15-Rom10:17); [15:21](https://ref.ly/Rom15:21); [1 Pet 2:24–25](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:24-1Pet2:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:13–ISA 53:12
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 42:1-4 (ID: `16339@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 52:14 (id: 16510)

were amazed: No one expected that the rescuer would suffer and die.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:14

## Isaiah 52:14–15 (id: 16509)

Despite the servant’s greatness, the actual way he would appear on earth would shock people.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:14–ISA 52:15

## Isaiah 52:15 (id: 16511)

startle many nations: They would be amazed that a rescuer would appear so weak and helpless and would stand speechless. • What they will see and what they will understand will be in complete contrast to anything they had previously imagined.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 52:15

## Isaiah 53:1 (id: 16524)

our message: The identity of the speaker has been debated—the main possibilities are (1\) a faithful remnant of Israel, and (2\) Isaiah himself. Most likely, Isaiah the prophet was speaking for and with Israel. • powerful arm: God’s strength, so dramatically described in the previous chapters (see [50:2](https://ref.ly/Isa50:2); [51:5](https://ref.ly/Isa51:5), [9](https://ref.ly/Isa51:9); [52:10](https://ref.ly/Isa52:10)), would actually manifest itself in weakness and apparent helplessness through the servant’s humiliation and exaltation (see [1 Cor 1:27–30](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:27-1Cor1:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:1

## Isaiah 53:2 (id: 16525)

a tender green shoot . . . in dry ground: Such a plant is vulnerable to extinction (cp. [37:27](https://ref.ly/Isa37:27)). It can hardly stay alive for itself, let alone provide anything for anyone else. • nothing beautiful or majestic: The servant appeared to have no greatness or self\-evident royal splendor (see [52:13–15](https://ref.ly/Isa52:13-Isa52:15)). • nothing to attract us to him: People like their leaders to be physically attractive and personally charismatic. The servant would be neither.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:2

## Isaiah 53:3 (id: 16526)

a man of sorrows, acquainted with deepest grief (or *a man of pains, acquainted with illness*): The servant would fully experience the effects of sin and the Fall. • we did not care: Because people would fail to see how such a weak, insignificant person could do anything beneficial for them, they would be unconcerned about his suffering.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:3

## Isaiah 53:4 (id: 16527)

The callous world would assume that the servant somehow brought his suffering on himself, never realizing that he was suffering for them. • troubles . . . punishment: These descriptions of the servant’s humiliation contrast with the descriptions of his exaltation.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:4

## Isaiah 53:5 (id: 16528)

he was pierced: See also [Zech 12:10](https://ref.ly/Zech12:10). • crushed . . . beaten . . . whipped: These were typically punishments for crimes. Sin is a crime against God. • be whole: Hebrew shalom, usually translated “peace.” *Shalom* means to experience wholeness in body, in mind, and in relationships with others. The servant would be injured so that humanity can be whole and healthy in all aspects of life (see also [Isa 57:18](https://ref.ly/Isa57:18)). We do not need to suffer divine condemnation for our sins because the servant has already done so (see [Gal 1:4](https://ref.ly/Gal1:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:5

## Isaiah 53:6 (id: 16529)

strayed away . . . left God’s paths: These are metaphors for sin (see also [Rom 3:10–18](https://ref.ly/Rom3:10-Rom3:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:6

## Isaiah 53:7 (id: 16531)

See [1 Pet 2:21–25](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:21-1Pet2:25) for the fulfillment of this prophecy in Jesus Christ.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:7

## Isaiah 53:7–8 (id: 16530)

The Ethiopian eunuch was reading this passage when Philip met him ([Acts 8:32–33](https://ref.ly/Acts8:32-Acts8:33)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:7–ISA 53:8

## Isaiah 53:8 (id: 16532)

Unjustly condemned: The servant will be given no legal protection or proper defense. • cut short in midstream: To die in midlife was understood to be God’s judgment.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:8

## Isaiah 53:9 (id: 16533)

no wrong . . . never deceived anyone: See [1 Pet 2:21–25](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:21-1Pet2:25). • in a rich man’s grave: Literally *he was with the rich in his death* (see [Matt 27:57–61](https://ref.ly/Matt27:57-Matt27:61)). Although the Bible often considers riches as a blessing from God, it regularly condemns the rich as crooked and oppressive. The point here might be ironic: This good man would be buried with oppressors.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:9

## Isaiah 53:10 (id: 16521)

The servant’s grief would accomplish a greater good; the forgiveness and reconciliation of sinful humanity. Note also God’s good plan to prosper and exalt the servant. • when his life is made an offering for sin: The suffering of the servant provided a substitute for others, just as the animal sacrifices in the Temple did. • Having many descendants and enjoying a long life are rewards for godly and wise living (see [Prov 3:2](https://ref.ly/Prov3:2); [17:6](https://ref.ly/Prov17:6); [20:7](https://ref.ly/Prov20:7)). Because the servant left his fate in his God’s hands, he would receive eternal rewards from the God who vindicates the righteous (see [Phil 2:9–11](https://ref.ly/Phil2:9-Phil2:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:10

## Isaiah 53:10–12 (id: 16520)

The final stanza of the poem first explains why the servant suffered and was treated unjustly in the place of others; it then explains what the result of that obedience would be.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:10–ISA 53:12

## Isaiah 53:11 (id: 16522)

his experience (literally *his knowledge*): This clearly does not refer to intellectual knowledge but to all that the servant would experience in his obedience, suffering, and intimate relationship with God. • The servant’s righteous obedience enables people to be put right with God (see [Gen 15:6](https://ref.ly/Gen15:6); [Rom 5:18–19](https://ref.ly/Rom5:18-Rom5:19)), for he will bear all their sins.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:11

## Isaiah 53:12 (id: 16523)

the honors: See [Phil 2:9–11](https://ref.ly/Phil2:9-Phil2:11). • He was counted among the rebels: *Rebels* (Hebrew poshe‘im) is a stronger word than *sinners* and is a key word in Isaiah. It refers to those who are in willful defiance of a lawful authority, in this case, God. • interceded for rebels: The servant would pray for sinners in the midst of his suffering (see [Exod 32:30](https://ref.ly/Exod32:30); [Luke 23:34](https://ref.ly/Luke23:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 53:12

## Isaiah 54:1 (id: 16544)

In the ancient world, a woman who had never given birth after being married for a time would be ashamed. Isaiah compares Jerusalem to a barren woman who rejoices at the long\-awaited blessing of children (see [Gal 4:27](https://ref.ly/Gal4:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:1

## Isaiah 54:1–3 (id: 16535)

The prophet encourages Jerusalem, likened to a barren woman, to rejoice because its fate was rapidly changing. She would have so many children that she would outgrow her home (see [Gal 4:27](https://ref.ly/Gal4:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:1–ISA 54:3

## Isaiah 54:1–17 (id: 16534)

Salvation flows from the vindication of the suffering servant. The promises mentioned here go beyond the return from Babylonian exile and apply to the coming of Jesus Christ, the extension of the kingdom to the church, the benefits of the second coming of Jesus Christ as the bridegroom of the church, and the new Jerusalem.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:1–ISA 54:17

## Isaiah 54:1–55.13 (id: 16536)

This is an invitation to participate in the restoration to God’s favor made possible through the ministry of the promised servant.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:1–ISA 55:13

## Isaiah 54:3 (id: 16545)

Israel’s descendants (cp. [53:10](https://ref.ly/Isa53:10)) would occupy other nations in fulfillment of God’s promise to Abraham ([Gen 22:17](https://ref.ly/Gen22:17)) and to Jacob ([Gen 28:14](https://ref.ly/Gen28:14)). • As desolation took place ([Isa 6:11](https://ref.ly/Isa6:11); [14:21](https://ref.ly/Isa14:21)), the people of God would inherit the earth and resettle the ruined cities ([51:6](https://ref.ly/Isa51:6); [52:10](https://ref.ly/Isa52:10); [65:17](https://ref.ly/Isa65:17); see also [Matt 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5); [Rom 4:13](https://ref.ly/Rom4:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:3

## Isaiah 54:5 (id: 16546)

Creator . . . husband: The Lord committed himself to the abandoned woman (his people in exile) as her maker ([44:24](https://ref.ly/Isa44:24)) and husband (see also [62:4–5](https://ref.ly/Isa62:4-Isa62:5); [Hos 2:19–20](https://ref.ly/Hos2:19-Hos2:20)). • The Redeemer transforms misery into freedom and fulfillment (see also [Isa 41:14](https://ref.ly/Isa41:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:5

## Isaiah 54:7–8 (id: 16547)

The pain of separation would be brief compared to the depth of the renewal of love and compassion. • The Lord abandoned Israel in exile for a little while because of the people’s sins. • everlasting love: The Lord is eternally committed to his people, making the seventy\-year punishment of exile seem short indeed (see [25:1](https://ref.ly/Isa25:1); [Hos 2:1](https://ref.ly/Hos2:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:7–ISA 54:8

## Isaiah 54:9 (id: 16548)

The Exile was similar in both drama and trauma to the flood in the time of Noah. In both instances, people sinned grievously against the Lord, but the Lord renewed his commitment to creation (after Noah’s flood) and to his people (after the Exile).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:9

## Isaiah 54:10 (id: 16537)

God’s faithful love for his people endures despite their unfaithfulness. • God’s covenant of blessing was the assurance of his presence, resulting in wholeness, blessing, and protection. It replaces the shame and disgrace of the Exile (see [Ezek 34:25](https://ref.ly/Ezek34:25); [37:26](https://ref.ly/Ezek37:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:10

## Isaiah 54:11 (id: 16539)

The Lord himself would rebuild the city (see [Heb 11:10](https://ref.ly/Heb11:10)). • Lapis lazuli is a semi\-precious stone.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:11

## Isaiah 54:11–17 (id: 16538)

This is a vision of the renewed Jerusalem as a city under God’s protection, a place of peace and righteousness (see [59:21–60:22](https://ref.ly/Isa59:21-Isa60:22)). This section forms the background of John’s vision of the new Jerusalem ([Rev 21:10–21](https://ref.ly/Rev21:10-Rev21:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:11–ISA 54:17

## Isaiah 54:13 (id: 16540)

I will teach: Jesus alluded to this verse in [John 6:45](https://ref.ly/John6:45). • They will enjoy great peace*,* the benefits of God’s presence and protection ([Isa 53:5](https://ref.ly/Isa53:5); see [48:17–18](https://ref.ly/Isa48:17-Isa48:18); [54:10](https://ref.ly/Isa54:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:13

## Isaiah 54:14 (id: 16541)

Jerusalem would again be a righteous city, secure under a government that is just and fair (see[1:26](https://ref.ly/Isa1:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:14

## Isaiah 54:15 (id: 16542)

God gives assurance that no nation can defeat his people . The Lord has promised to protect them, just as he had promised Abraham ([Gen 12:3](https://ref.ly/Gen12:3); see [Isa 49:25](https://ref.ly/Isa49:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:15

## Isaiah 54:17 (id: 16543)

no weapon . . . will succeed . . . accuse you . . . vindication: God will protect his people in war and in the courtroom. • These benefits are enjoyed by the servants of the Lord: Only the true children of God—people who come out of Israel and the nations—will enjoy the promised blessings of the age to come that God establishes.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 54:17

## Isaiah 55:1 (id: 16554)

thirsty . . . wine or milk: The invitation to eat and drink is similar to Wisdom’s call in [Prov 9:5](https://ref.ly/Prov9:5). The image promises the slaking of thirst not only by water but also by more costly items such as wine and milk. John applied a similar theme to Jesus Christ ([John 4:14](https://ref.ly/John4:14); [6:27](https://ref.ly/John6:27), [35](https://ref.ly/John6:35); [7:37](https://ref.ly/John7:37); [Rev 21:6](https://ref.ly/Rev21:6); [22:17](https://ref.ly/Rev22:17)). • it’s all free: Reconciliation with God is for anyone and has no cost.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:1

## Isaiah 55:1–13 (id: 16549)

This final chapter of the prophecies of comfort (chs [40–55](https://ref.ly/Isa40:1-Isa55:13)) summarizes the section’s prominent themes: blessing, covenant, witness, word, nations, glory, forgiveness, and joy.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:1–ISA 55:13

## Isaiah 55:2 (id: 16555)

Listen to me . . . eat what is good: Responding positively to God satisfies one’s spiritual, social, and physical being (see [1:19](https://ref.ly/Isa1:19); [58:13–14](https://ref.ly/Isa58:13-Isa58:14); [Prov 4:10](https://ref.ly/Prov4:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:2

## Isaiah 55:3 (id: 16556)

Come to me. . . . Listen . . . find life: Those who respond obediently to God’s word find eternal life (see also [55:11](https://ref.ly/Isa55:11)). • an everlasting covenant . . . I promised to David: King David received a special covenant from God, a promise to preserve his kingly line (see [2 Sam 7:15–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:15-2Sam7:16)). David’s dynasty was eternally confirmed in the kingship of the Messiah, Jesus Christ (see [Isa 9:6–7](https://ref.ly/Isa9:6-Isa9:7); [11:1–16](https://ref.ly/Isa11:1-Isa11:16); [Acts 2:22–36](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22-Acts2:36); [13:34](https://ref.ly/Acts13:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:3

## Isaiah 55:6 (id: 16558)

while you can find him: When God graciously extends an invitation to salvation, people must respond ([65:1](https://ref.ly/Isa65:1); [Jer 29:13–14](https://ref.ly/Jer29:13-Jer29:14); [Hos 5:6](https://ref.ly/Hos5:6); [10:12](https://ref.ly/Hos10:12)). Those who do not seek him at such times risk never having the opportunity again.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:6

## Isaiah 55:6–9 (id: 16557)

The prophet calls for a response while the time is right.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:6–ISA 55:9

## Isaiah 55:7 (id: 16559)

Let the wicked change . . . turn to the Lord: True conversion demands a change of how we live in favor of God’s requirements (see [1:16–17](https://ref.ly/Isa1:16-Isa1:17); [30:15](https://ref.ly/Isa30:15); [59:20](https://ref.ly/Isa59:20)). • have mercy on them: God’s compassion reaches out to the needy and finds them where they are. • he will forgive generously: Forgiveness of sin is foundational to the good news of redemption (see [Eph 1:7](https://ref.ly/Eph1:7); [Col 1:14](https://ref.ly/Col1:14); see also [Pss 32:1](https://ref.ly/Ps32:1); [86:5](https://ref.ly/Ps86:5); [99:8](https://ref.ly/Ps99:8); [103:2–5](https://ref.ly/Ps103:2-Ps103:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:7

## Isaiah 55:8–9 (id: 16560)

My thoughts are nothing like your thoughts: God’s plans are marvelous ([Ps 92:5](https://ref.ly/Ps92:5); cp. [Ps 94:11](https://ref.ly/Ps94:11)). God’s creatures, including humans, can never fully understand the Creator’s thoughts, but his revelation through his messengers gives great insight and knowledge of some of the things he will do.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:8–ISA 55:9

## Isaiah 55:10–11 (id: 16550)

The Creator not only sends rain and snow but also his word (Hebrew dabar). In this context, dabar means his *will* or *plan* (see [14:24](https://ref.ly/Isa14:24); [40:8](https://ref.ly/Isa40:8)). God’s written word, as an expression of God’s plan, accomplishes his purposes. God is effective in whatever he does (see [14:26–27](https://ref.ly/Isa14:26-Isa14:27); [46:10](https://ref.ly/Isa46:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:10–ISA 55:11

## Isaiah 55:12 (id: 16552)

Joy is found in being redeemed from bondage. • Godly people experience an inner peace not known to the wicked ([48:22](https://ref.ly/Isa48:22)). • mountains and hills . . . trees of the field: Creation participates in the freedom of the children of God ([44:23](https://ref.ly/Isa44:23); [49:11](https://ref.ly/Isa49:11), [13](https://ref.ly/Isa49:13); see [Rom 8:19–23](https://ref.ly/Rom8:19-Rom8:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:12

## Isaiah 55:12–13 (id: 16551)

The prophet encourages his people to forget the past, to leave Babylon, and to accept the perspective of the coming age.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:12–ISA 55:13

## Isaiah 55:13 (id: 16553)

Redemption is like the transformation from desert to forest (see also [35:1](https://ref.ly/Isa35:1); [41:19](https://ref.ly/Isa41:19); [60:13](https://ref.ly/Isa60:13)). • great honor to the Lord’s name: God’s glory will be more and more visible to humanity as his redemption takes effect.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 55:13

## Isaiah 56:1 (id: 16565)

Be just and fair: A key aspect of the message of chs [1–39](https://ref.ly/Isa1:1-Isa39:8) is the call for justice in relationship with others and God. True godliness comes only through having character that is shaped by the character of God, which only happens by understanding and consistently applying God’s word. • I am coming soon: This statement summarizes the message of chs [40–55](https://ref.ly/Isa40:1-Isa55:13), that the Lord is creating a world of harmony, peace, restoration, vindication, and the removal of enemies ([46:13](https://ref.ly/Isa46:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:1

## Isaiah 56:1–8 (id: 16562)

This section summarizes chs [1–55](https://ref.ly/Isa1:1-Isa55:13) with an invitation to the outcasts to participate in God’s redemption.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:1–ISA 56:8

## Isaiah 56:1–66.24 (id: 16561)

This last major division of the book of Isaiah brings together themes from chs [1–39](https://ref.ly/Isa1:1-Isa39:8) (sin, justice and righteousness, responsibility, vengeance and vindication) and chs [40–55](https://ref.ly/Isa40:1-Isa55:13) (salvation, the age to come).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:1

## Isaiah 56:2 (id: 16566)

Blessed: Cp. [30:18](https://ref.ly/Isa30:18); [32:20](https://ref.ly/Isa32:20); see also [Pss 1:1](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1); [119:1](https://ref.ly/Ps119:1); [Matt 5:3](https://ref.ly/Matt5:3). • The Sabbath*,* as a sign of the covenant ([Exod 31:13–17](https://ref.ly/Exod31:13-Exod31:17)), is God’s gift to his people; it belongs to this age as well as to the age to come ([Isa 56:4](https://ref.ly/Isa56:4), [6](https://ref.ly/Isa56:6); [58:13–14](https://ref.ly/Isa58:13-Isa58:14); see [Heb 4:1–13](https://ref.ly/Heb4:1-Heb4:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:2

## Isaiah 56:3 (id: 16568)

Foreigners who commit themselves to the Lord would become full participants in the covenant community. Previously, their participation had been carefully regulated ([Deut 23:3](https://ref.ly/Deut23:3), [7–8](https://ref.ly/Deut23:7-Deut23:8)). • eunuchs: In the past, an emasculated person was excluded from the community ([Deut 23:1](https://ref.ly/Deut23:1)). Both eunuchs and foreigners had no share in Israel’s holiness and were considered marginal to God’s kingdom. In the age to come, God would bring to the center those who had previously been marginalized (cp. [Matt 20:16](https://ref.ly/Matt20:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:3

## Isaiah 56:3–7 (id: 16567)

The blessing ([56:2](https://ref.ly/Isa56:2)) would extend to eunuchs and to the Gentiles.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:3–ISA 56:7

## Isaiah 56:4 (id: 16569)

The Sabbath is a sign of the covenant ([Exod 31:13–17](https://ref.ly/Exod31:13-Exod31:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:4

## Isaiah 56:5 (id: 16570)

within the walls of my house: Those previously excluded would have a place in God’s presence. • a memorial and a name: Everlasting existence in God’s presence is better than the blessing of physical descendants.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:5

## Isaiah 56:6 (id: 16571)

The essential ingredient for covenant fellowship is love for God ([Deut 6:5](https://ref.ly/Deut6:5); [30:20](https://ref.ly/Deut30:20); [Matt 22:34–38](https://ref.ly/Matt22:34-Matt22:38)). • Keeping the Sabbath is a sign of keeping the covenant itself (see [Exod 31:13–17](https://ref.ly/Exod31:13-Exod31:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:6

## Isaiah 56:7 (id: 16572)

burnt offerings and sacrifices: God had previously rejected sinful Israel’s expressions of piety ([1:11–13](https://ref.ly/Isa1:11-Isa1:13)) but would welcome offerings from righteous Gentiles or foreigners. Nationality is worth little without true piety. • a house of prayer for all nations: The Lord would open the doors of the Temple to all nations (see [2:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2-Isa2:4)). Jesus rebuked the people for desecrating the Temple and for preventing it from functioning as the house of prayer ([Matt 21:13](https://ref.ly/Matt21:13); [Mark 11:17](https://ref.ly/Mark11:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:7

## Isaiah 56:8 (id: 16573)

The outcasts of Israel were those dispersed among the nations as the result of the Exile (see also [11:12](https://ref.ly/Isa11:12)). • The others would be eunuchs and Gentiles ([56:3–7](https://ref.ly/Isa56:3-Isa56:7); see also [57:19](https://ref.ly/Isa57:19); [John 10:16](https://ref.ly/John10:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:8

## Isaiah 56:9 (id: 16575)

Wild animals are here a metaphor for the hostile nations surrounding Judah.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:9

## Isaiah 56:9–57.13 (id: 16574)

This is a reflection on the prevalence of evil among God’s people; they were greedy ([56:9–12](https://ref.ly/Isa56:9-Isa56:12)), hostile to the righteous ([57:1–2](https://ref.ly/Isa57:1-Isa57:2)), and idolatrous ([57:3–13](https://ref.ly/Isa57:3-Isa57:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:9–ISA 57:13

## Isaiah 56:10 (id: 16563)

The leaders of Israel failed to guide and protect God’s people from the sins that led to the Exile. • sleeping and dreaming: See [29:10](https://ref.ly/Isa29:10).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:10

## Isaiah 56:11 (id: 16564)

ignorant shepherds: Israel’s leaders did not know how to rule in a godly way (see also [Ezek 34:1–6](https://ref.ly/Ezek34:1-Ezek34:6)). By contrast, the Lord is the faithful Shepherd of his people ([Isa 40:11](https://ref.ly/Isa40:11)). • all following their own path: They had no concern for God or his standards of godly leadership (see also [53:6](https://ref.ly/Isa53:6)). • personal gain: Cp. [33:15](https://ref.ly/Isa33:15).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 56:11

## Isaiah 57:1 (id: 16584)

the evil to come: Judgment that would come on the wicked nations. • protecting them: At times, God allows the godly to die in order to protect them from harsher times to come.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:1

## Isaiah 57:1–2 (id: 16576)

This is a lament for the righteous who suffer in a wicked society.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:1–ISA 57:2

## Isaiah 57:2 (id: 16587)

The wicked would not be able to rest in peace ([57:21](https://ref.ly/Isa57:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:2

## Isaiah 57:3 (id: 16588)

witches’ children . . . adulterers and prostitutes: Baal religion, which flourished in Israel before the Exile (see [1:21–23](https://ref.ly/Isa1:21-Isa1:23)), included lewd sexual practices.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:3

## Isaiah 57:4 (id: 16589)

mock . . . sticking out your tongues: The wicked oppressed the righteous by their insults ([57:1–2](https://ref.ly/Isa57:1-Isa57:2); see also [28:9](https://ref.ly/Isa28:9), [14](https://ref.ly/Isa28:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:4

## Isaiah 57:5 (id: 16590)

beneath the oaks and under every green tree: Tree groves were commonly used as places of pagan worship (see [1:29–30](https://ref.ly/Isa1:29-Isa1:30)). • sacrifice your children: The horrible practice of child sacrifice was occasionally practiced in Israel (see [Ps 106:37–38](https://ref.ly/Ps106:37-Ps106:38)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:5

## Isaiah 57:6 (id: 16591)

Liquid offerings and grain offerings were believed to satisfy the basic needs of the gods and thus to earn their favor.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:6

## Isaiah 57:8 (id: 16592)

climbed into bed: The people of Israel had a sickening commitment to the fertility religions, which included sex as part of their rituals.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:8

## Isaiah 57:11 (id: 16577)

The people were living in fear of false gods instead of fearing the Lord (see [8:12–13](https://ref.ly/Isa8:12-Isa8:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:11

## Isaiah 57:12 (id: 16578)

The Lord did not consider the people’s so\-called good deeds (literally *righteousness;* see [59:16](https://ref.ly/Isa59:16)) to be truly righteous.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:12

## Isaiah 57:13 (id: 16579)

your idols . . . fall over: See study note on 40:18. • inherit the land: The Hebrew word translated land can also signify the whole earth (see [Pss 25:13](https://ref.ly/Ps25:13); [37:9](https://ref.ly/Ps37:9), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11), [22](https://ref.ly/Ps37:22), [29](https://ref.ly/Ps37:29), [34](https://ref.ly/Ps37:34); [Matt 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5)). • my holy mountain: God’s servants will enjoy God’s presence in Zion (see [Isa 2:2](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2); [56:7](https://ref.ly/Isa56:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:13
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 40:18 (ID: `16300@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 57:14–21 (id: 16580)

The Lord here promises to be present with the humble, to heal them, and to grant them his peace. The promise extends to all the citizens of Zion, both Jews and Gentiles. The Holy One comes to the humble with an all\-inclusive offer of salvation, while dealing justly with the wicked.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:14–ISA 57:21

## Isaiah 57:15 (id: 16581)

Even though God is the high and lofty one*,* he promises to dwell with the humble.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:15

## Isaiah 57:18 (id: 16582)

I will heal them anyway: Salvation is by God’s grace (see [19:22](https://ref.ly/Isa19:22); [30:26](https://ref.ly/Isa30:26); [53:5](https://ref.ly/Isa53:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:18

## Isaiah 57:19 (id: 16583)

words of praise: God’s redemption should bring a response of praise from its recipients. • both near and far: Both Gentiles and Jews are included (see [56:3](https://ref.ly/Isa56:3); [John 10:16](https://ref.ly/John10:16); [Eph 2:17](https://ref.ly/Eph2:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:19

## Isaiah 57:20 (id: 16585)

restless sea . . . never still: Those who live in constant opposition to God (see [Pss 46:3](https://ref.ly/Ps46:3), [6](https://ref.ly/Ps46:6); [93:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps93:3-Ps93:4)) do not enjoy inner quiet because they are not at peace with God ([Isa 30:15](https://ref.ly/Isa30:15); [32:17](https://ref.ly/Isa32:17)). • churns up mud and dirt: Their activity has little productivity (see [Ps 40:2](https://ref.ly/Ps40:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:20

## Isaiah 57:21 (id: 16586)

no peace: Cp. [57:2](https://ref.ly/Isa57:2); see also [48:22](https://ref.ly/Isa48:22).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 57:21

## Isaiah 58:1–4 (id: 16593)

This is a charge against religious Israelites who were pleased with themselves because of their religious activities.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:1–ISA 58:4

## Isaiah 58:2 (id: 16598)

they act so pious (literally *they seek me*): They may have been truly committed to a religious form, but they failed to truly meet God in their religious activities.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:2

## Isaiah 58:3 (id: 16599)

Fasting should be a time of self\-deprivation in order to focus on God and pleasing him ([Lev 16:29](https://ref.ly/Lev16:29); see [Zech 7:5](https://ref.ly/Zech7:5)). However, these people were only interested in pleasing themselves and continuing in their sins.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:3

## Isaiah 58:5 (id: 16600)

This is a satirical portrayal of the people’s fasting as mere external piety without repentance and righteous acts. Ritualistic and insincere fasting is nothing but pomp. • Wearing burlap and ashes are expressions of sorrow and mourning. • please the Lord? The people erroneously believed that the Lord would bless them, if only they performed the right rituals.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:5

## Isaiah 58:6–7 (id: 16601)

True fasting creates an awareness of injustice and oppression and prompts the practitioner to reach out to help the needy in their struggles (see [42:7](https://ref.ly/Isa42:7); [Matt 25:35–36](https://ref.ly/Matt25:35-Matt25:36); [Jas 1:27](https://ref.ly/Jas1:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:6–ISA 58:7

## Isaiah 58:8 (id: 16602)

your salvation (literally *your light*): The light of the coming age (see [42:6–7](https://ref.ly/Isa42:6-Isa42:7); [60:1–3](https://ref.ly/Isa60:1-Isa60:3)) will dawn on those who turn fully to the Lord. The night of divine judgment and oppression will be over. • your wounds: The nation of Israel was wounded when they were conquered and sent into exile. • protect you from behind: See also [52:12](https://ref.ly/Isa52:12).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:8

## Isaiah 58:9 (id: 16603)

the Lord will answer: Cp. [1:15](https://ref.ly/Isa1:15); see also [19:22](https://ref.ly/Isa19:22). • Stop . . . spreading vicious rumors: God calls for an end to acts and words that destroy relationships (see [Prov 6:12–14](https://ref.ly/Prov6:12-Prov6:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:9

## Isaiah 58:10 (id: 16594)

your light . . . as bright as noon: God would rescue and vindicate his people (see [Job 11:17](https://ref.ly/Job11:17); [Ps 37:6](https://ref.ly/Ps37:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:10

## Isaiah 58:12 (id: 16595)

a rebuilder of walls: Nehemiah would later fulfill this promise (see [Neh 2:17](https://ref.ly/Neh2:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:12

## Isaiah 58:13 (id: 16596)

Like the practice of fasting, the Sabbath was intended to be an expression of self\-denial and worship. It consists of delighting in the Lord, trusting him to provide for one’s needs while abstaining from work, and living in obedience to his will.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:13

## Isaiah 58:14 (id: 16597)

As people honor God through obedience, they themselves will be honored by God. • the inheritance I promised to your ancestor Jacob: The promised inheritance includes living with many descendants in the holy land and enjoying God’s presence, blessing, and protection ([Gen 31:3](https://ref.ly/Gen31:3); [35:9–12](https://ref.ly/Gen35:9-Gen35:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 58:14

## Isaiah 59:1 (id: 16611)

not too weak: The delay in their rescue could not be attributed to an inherent weakness in the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:1

## Isaiah 59:1–8 (id: 16605)

The people complained that the Lord could not rescue them, but the real problem was that they had not repented ([59:20](https://ref.ly/Isa59:20)) and were still living in sin.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:1–ISA 59:8

## Isaiah 59:1–20 (id: 16604)

The Lord alone can and will usher in his salvation. Like a warrior, he will break into the world to avenge himself on his enemies and to vindicate his holy people.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:1–ISA 59:20

## Isaiah 59:2 (id: 16613)

your sins . . . cut you off: The Israelites, like all people ([Rom 3:15–17](https://ref.ly/Rom3:15-Rom3:17)), had sinned, which resulted in alienation from God (he has turned away).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:2

## Isaiah 59:4 (id: 16614)

being fair and honest: Israel did not practice these qualities that are part of God’s nature and that he expects from people ([1:21](https://ref.ly/Isa1:21); see [25:1](https://ref.ly/Isa25:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:4

## Isaiah 59:5–6 (id: 16615)

The images of deadly snakes and spiders’ webs represent plans designed to destroy others’ lives and relationships.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:5–ISA 59:6

## Isaiah 59:7–8 (id: 16616)

Paul quotes from these verses in his description of the depravity of all people ([Rom 3:15–17](https://ref.ly/Rom3:15-Rom3:17)). • Misery and destruction: The people lamented being victims of oppression ([Isa 51:19](https://ref.ly/Isa51:19)), yet they were oppressors themselves.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:7–ISA 59:8

## Isaiah 59:9–15 (id: 16617)

Israel’s history of rebellion was well established. The prophet here confesses the nation’s sins and laments that they could not apprehend the light of God’s salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:9–ISA 59:15

## Isaiah 59:10 (id: 16606)

people without eyes: See [6:10](https://ref.ly/Isa6:10); [Deut 28:29](https://ref.ly/Deut28:29).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:10

## Isaiah 59:11–14 (id: 16607)

The people growl and moan with longing for redemption, finally coming to terms with their sinfulness.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:11–ISA 59:14

## Isaiah 59:15–17 (id: 16608)

The Lord goes out as a warrior intent on achieving victory against the wicked (cp. [Eph 6:14](https://ref.ly/Eph6:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:15–ISA 59:17

## Isaiah 59:18 (id: 16609)

repay his enemies: The Lord will dole out righteous retribution on the whole earth. His justice requires people to be judged for the evil they have done (see also [3:9–11](https://ref.ly/Isa3:9-Isa3:11); [13:9](https://ref.ly/Isa13:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:18

## Isaiah 59:19 (id: 16610)

In the west . . . in the east: I.e., in all parts of the world.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:19

## Isaiah 59:21 (id: 16612)

The members of the new community have the Spirit*,* and they know and practice God’s word (see also [Ezek 36:24–28](https://ref.ly/Ezek36:24-Ezek36:28)). The Lord promises to regenerate the children by his Spirit and bring them into the covenant of obedience and love for the Lord ([Joel 2:28](https://ref.ly/Joel2:28); [Acts 2:39](https://ref.ly/Acts2:39)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 59:21

## Isaiah 60:1–3 (id: 16629)

God will come to be with his people and will transform Zion’s destiny from the darkness as black as night caused by sin and judgment.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:1–ISA 60:3

## Isaiah 60:3 (id: 16642)

The transformation of all nations and mighty kings will be so radical that all kingdoms will take notice and be drawn to God through his people (see also [Rev 21:24](https://ref.ly/Rev21:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:3

## Isaiah 60:5–7 (id: 16643)

Zion’s losses from warfare will be restored by the wealth of many lands*;* foreign nations will be eager to make a contribution ([60:11](https://ref.ly/Isa60:11); [61:6](https://ref.ly/Isa61:6); [66:12](https://ref.ly/Isa66:12); see [Rev 21:26](https://ref.ly/Rev21:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:5–ISA 60:7

## Isaiah 60:6 (id: 16644)

Midian and Ephah were Midianite tribes located southeast of Israel. • Sheba was a region in southern Arabia (see [1 Kgs 10:1–2](https://ref.ly/1Kgs10:1-1Kgs10:2)) famed for frankincense ([Jer 6:20](https://ref.ly/Jer6:20)). • These were real nations—the restoration would be a historical reality, not just an idealistic vision. Many nations would submit themselves to and worship the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:6

## Isaiah 60:7 (id: 16645)

Kedar was a tribe in Arabia ([21:16–17](https://ref.ly/Isa21:16-Isa21:17)). • Nebaioth was an Ishmaelite tribe. • I will make my Temple glorious: The glory of God will be even more evident than it was in Solomon’s Temple (see [6:1–5](https://ref.ly/Isa6:1-Isa6:5); [Hag 2:9](https://ref.ly/Hag2:9); [Rev 21:11](https://ref.ly/Rev21:11), [22](https://ref.ly/Rev21:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:7

## Isaiah 60:9 (id: 16646)

filled you with splendor: See [Rev 21:26](https://ref.ly/Rev21:26).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:9

## Isaiah 60:10 (id: 16631)

their kings will serve you: God’s people who were previously humiliated ([2:11](https://ref.ly/Isa2:11)) will be exalted.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:10

## Isaiah 60:10–16 (id: 16630)

Those who previously oppressed the people of God will one day participate in restoring the holy city (see [2:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2-Isa2:4); [19:18–25](https://ref.ly/Isa19:18-Isa19:25); [Neh 2:8](https://ref.ly/Neh2:8); [Amos 9:12](https://ref.ly/Amos9:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:10–ISA 60:16

## Isaiah 60:11 (id: 16632)

There are two likely reasons for why the gates are not closed at night (see also [Rev 21:25](https://ref.ly/Rev21:25)): (1\) So much traffic will be coming into the city ([Isa 60:8–10](https://ref.ly/Isa60:8-Isa60:10)) that the gates will need to be open. (2\) The citizens of Zion will no longer need to fear enemies because the Lord is their protector ([60:18](https://ref.ly/Isa60:18)); the nations that remain will be serving the Lord and his people ([60:9](https://ref.ly/Isa60:9), [12](https://ref.ly/Isa60:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:11

## Isaiah 60:12 (id: 16633)

In the coming age, nations that refuse to obey God will be destroyed.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:12

## Isaiah 60:13 (id: 16634)

The Temple was God’s sanctuary*,* the symbol of his presence on earth. Believers now are the temple of God by the indwelling Spirit ([1 Cor 3:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:16)). We still await the fullness of God’s presence ([Rev 21:22](https://ref.ly/Rev21:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:13

## Isaiah 60:15 (id: 16635)

beautiful forever, a joy to all generations: This would be radical change from the conditions of the Exile in Babylon. Fulfillments of this prophecy include the Jews’ restoration from exile, the coming of Jesus Christ, and the inclusion of the Gentiles in the church. The final fulfillment awaits the glorious second coming of Jesus Christ, which will usher in the new Jerusalem.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:15

## Isaiah 60:17 (id: 16637)

gold . . . silver . . . bronze . . . iron: These metals are for adornment and strength (cp. [54:11](https://ref.ly/Isa54:11); [Rev 21:15–21](https://ref.ly/Rev21:15-Rev21:21)). • Peace and righteousness will bring harmony and blessing among people and with God.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:17

## Isaiah 60:17–20 (id: 16636)

These verses portray Zion’s future grandeur (cp. [Rev 21:10–22:4](https://ref.ly/Rev21:10-Rev22:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:17–ISA 60:20

## Isaiah 60:18 (id: 16638)

praise will be on the lips of all who enter there (literally *they will call your gates “praise”*): Entrance into the city of salvation will be through the metaphorical gates of praise to the Lord for his great salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:18

## Isaiah 60:19–20 (id: 16639)

Natural sources of light such as the sun and the moon will be as nothing in comparison to the brightness of God’s presence (see also [9:2](https://ref.ly/Isa9:2); [30:26](https://ref.ly/Isa30:26); [Zech 2:5](https://ref.ly/Zech2:5); [Rev 21:23–24](https://ref.ly/Rev21:23-Rev21:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:19–ISA 60:20

## Isaiah 60:21 (id: 16640)

The citizens of Zion will be righteous*,* enjoying a right relationship with God and with others ([Rev 21:27](https://ref.ly/Rev21:27)). • their land: Or *the entire earth* ([Isa 54:5](https://ref.ly/Isa54:5); [62:7](https://ref.ly/Isa62:7); [65:17](https://ref.ly/Isa65:17); [66:22](https://ref.ly/Isa66:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:21

## Isaiah 60:22 (id: 16641)

I, the Lord: The Lord identifies himself as the covenant God of Israel. His identity ensures that he will make it happen (see [27:3–4](https://ref.ly/Isa27:3-Isa27:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 60:22

## Isaiah 61:1 (id: 16649)

The presence of God’s Spirit ensures the success of the servant’s mission (see [11:1–5](https://ref.ly/Isa11:1-Isa11:5); [42:1](https://ref.ly/Isa42:1)). • The servant will restore and heal the marginalized poor and the brokenhearted (see [25:4](https://ref.ly/Isa25:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:1

## Isaiah 61:1–3 (id: 16647)
