The servant here proclaims the good news that his ministry will restore Zion. The Lord Jesus applied these words to his own mission ([Luke 4:18–19](https://ref.ly/Luke4:18-Luke4:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:1–ISA 61:3

## Isaiah 61:2 (id: 16650)

The time of the Lord’s favor is the day of God’s salvation (see [49:8](https://ref.ly/Isa49:8)). • the day of God’s anger: God now turns his wrath against the enemies of his people. It will be a day of righteous vengeance (see [34:8](https://ref.ly/Isa34:8); [63:3–4](https://ref.ly/Isa63:3-Isa63:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:2

## Isaiah 61:3 (id: 16651)

Putting ashes on one’s head was a sign of mourning (note the reversal of the judgment stated in [3:16–25](https://ref.ly/Isa3:16-Isa3:25)). Mourning would be replaced by joy. The words translated crown of beauty and ashes form a wordplay in Hebrew. • joyous blessing (literally *oil of gladness*): A face covered with oil was a sign of blessing and well\-being (see [Pss 45:8](https://ref.ly/Ps45:8); [133:2](https://ref.ly/Ps133:2)). • The remnant would start out as small offshoots but would grow into great oaks (see [Isa 60:21](https://ref.ly/Isa60:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:3

## Isaiah 61:6 (id: 16652)

priests . . . ministers: The nation would fulfill its original calling ([Exod 19:6](https://ref.ly/Exod19:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:6

## Isaiah 61:7 (id: 16653)

The people had suffered God’s wrath for their sins ([40:2](https://ref.ly/Isa40:2)); now they would receive a double share of God’s blessing.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:7

## Isaiah 61:8 (id: 16654)

Those who belong to the community of God’s people are to imitate the character of God, who loves justice (see [Mic 6:8](https://ref.ly/Mic6:8)) and hates wrongdoing ([Isa 33:15](https://ref.ly/Isa33:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:8

## Isaiah 61:9 (id: 16655)

Their descendants: The covenant will be effective from generation to generation. • The Lord has blessed them in fulfillment of his promise to Abraham ([Gen 12:1–2](https://ref.ly/Gen12:1-Gen12:2); see [Isa 65:23](https://ref.ly/Isa65:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:9

## Isaiah 61:10 (id: 16648)

clothing of salvation . . . robe of righteousness: With great joy God will clothe his people with the benefits of his salvation and righteousness (see [51:5](https://ref.ly/Isa51:5); [56:1](https://ref.ly/Isa56:1)), like a bridegroom . . . or a bride (see [49:18](https://ref.ly/Isa49:18); [62:5](https://ref.ly/Isa62:5); [Jer 2:32](https://ref.ly/Jer2:32); [7:34](https://ref.ly/Jer7:34); [16:9](https://ref.ly/Jer16:9); [25:10](https://ref.ly/Jer25:10); [33:11](https://ref.ly/Jer33:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 61:10

## Isaiah 62:1–12 (id: 16656)

The servant here commits himself to proclaiming the good news continuously until the glory of Zion is realized.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:1–ISA 62:12

## Isaiah 62:2 (id: 16659)

The real beauty and glory of God’s people would not be seen in earthly treasures or a rebuilt city but would shine forth from their righteousness. Others would be drawn by this divine gift. • A new name reflects the change in Zion’s status (see [62:4](https://ref.ly/Isa62:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:2

## Isaiah 62:4 (id: 16660)

The Forsaken City: In the Exile, the Lord abandoned his people to the judgment they deserved ([54:7](https://ref.ly/Isa54:7)). • The Bride of God: The people will be “married” to the Lord—an appropriate image for the close covenant relationship ([54:5](https://ref.ly/Isa54:5); [Hos 1–3](https://ref.ly/Hos1:1-Hos3:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:4

## Isaiah 62:6–7 (id: 16661)

The watchmen probably represent the prophets. • they will pray day and night: They will continually seek the full restoration and blessing of Zion, unlike the destructive watchmen of [56:10](https://ref.ly/Isa56:10).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:6–ISA 62:7

## Isaiah 62:8 (id: 16662)

The Lord swore an oath just as he did when he had sworn an oath to Noah ([Gen 8:20–9:17](https://ref.ly/Gen8:20-Gen9:17)), to Abraham ([Gen 22:16](https://ref.ly/Gen22:16); see also [Luke 1:73](https://ref.ly/Luke1:73); [Heb 6:13](https://ref.ly/Heb6:13)), and to David ([Ps 89:3](https://ref.ly/Ps89:3)). • I will never again hand you over: In order to punish and purge a remnant from his people, God had intentionally brought in the Assyrians and Babylonians to decimate them (see [Isa 6:12–13](https://ref.ly/Isa6:12-Isa6:13)). He would never do this again.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:8

## Isaiah 62:9 (id: 16663)

The people would eat and drink the fruit of their labor ([65:13](https://ref.ly/Isa65:13), [22](https://ref.ly/Isa65:22); see [Lev 23:39–40](https://ref.ly/Lev23:39-Lev23:40); [Deut 14:22–26](https://ref.ly/Deut14:22-Deut14:26)). This is the opposite of what happened when God judged them (see [Deut 28:38–40](https://ref.ly/Deut28:38-Deut28:40); [Amos 5:11](https://ref.ly/Amos5:11); [Mic 6:14–15](https://ref.ly/Mic6:14-Mic6:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:9

## Isaiah 62:10 (id: 16658)

highway: See also [40:3](https://ref.ly/Isa40:3); [57:14](https://ref.ly/Isa57:14). • A flag for all the nations to see is a signal that directs foreigners to come to Zion for God’s salvation. Earlier, a similar signal was used to call for the nations to attack Judah ([5:26](https://ref.ly/Isa5:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:10

## Isaiah 62:10–12 (id: 16657)

This call to prepare for God’s coming salvation combines elements from all parts of Isaiah: the proclamation (the signal or banner, see [5:26](https://ref.ly/Isa5:26)), the preparation of the road ([40:3](https://ref.ly/Isa40:3); [57:14](https://ref.ly/Isa57:14)), the coming of God with his reward ([40:5](https://ref.ly/Isa40:5), [9–10](https://ref.ly/Isa40:9-Isa40:10)), and the holy and redeemed citizenry ([35:8–10](https://ref.ly/Isa35:8-Isa35:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 62:10–ISA 62:12

## Isaiah 63:1 (id: 16672)

The Lord’s robes are stained red with blood ([63:3](https://ref.ly/Isa63:3); cp. [Rev 19:13](https://ref.ly/Rev19:13)). • The name Bozrah (Hebrew botsrah) is a wordplay on the verb batsar (“gather grapes”).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:1

## Isaiah 63:1–6 (id: 16664)

The judgment of Edom typifies God’s judgment of all the nations (see also [34:5–15](https://ref.ly/Isa34:5-Isa34:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:1–ISA 63:6

## Isaiah 63:2 (id: 16673)

The term red (Hebrew ’adom) is a wordplay on the name *Edom.*

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:2

## Isaiah 63:4 (id: 16674)

the time . . . to avenge my people: See study note on 34:8. • to ransom: See study note on 43:1.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:4
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 34:8 (ID: `16214@TyndaleStudyNotes`); Isaiah 43:1 (ID: `16358@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 63:6 (id: 16675)

made them stagger: The wicked nations would be forced to drink from the intoxicating cup of God’s wrath ([49:26](https://ref.ly/Isa49:26); [51:17](https://ref.ly/Isa51:17), [21](https://ref.ly/Isa51:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:6

## Isaiah 63:7 (id: 16677)

unfailing love . . . all he has done . . . his great goodness: The whole history of God’s care for his people demonstrates his compassion, provision, and protection.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:7

## Isaiah 63:7–14 (id: 16676)

The prophet reflects on Israel’s past, how God showed his unfailing love and how his people alternatively rebelled against him, suffered hardship, returned to the Lord, and experienced his blessing.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:7–ISA 63:14

## Isaiah 63:8 (id: 16678)

They are my very own people: God’s possession of and commitment to his people was central to the covenant (see [43:1](https://ref.ly/Isa43:1)). • they will not betray me: The Lord expected his own people to honor their relationship with him, unlike the nations, whose story is a history of treachery ([Gen 3–11](https://ref.ly/Gen3:1-Gen11:32)). But Israel, too, betrayed their God ([Isa 63:10](https://ref.ly/Isa63:10)). • their Savior: God rescued and protected his people (see [43:3](https://ref.ly/Isa43:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:8

## Isaiah 63:9 (id: 16679)

he also suffered: God identified with his suffering people, and their suffering brought him grief. Later, Jesus suffered on behalf of all humanity. • and he personally rescued them: e.g., see [Exod 12:25–33](https://ref.ly/Exod12:25-Exod12:33); [14:10–31](https://ref.ly/Exod14:10-Exod14:31); [23:20–23](https://ref.ly/Exod23:20-Exod23:23).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:9

## Isaiah 63:10 (id: 16665)

But they rebelled: See also [1:2](https://ref.ly/Isa1:2), [4](https://ref.ly/Isa1:4); [59:1–15](https://ref.ly/Isa59:1-Isa59:15); [Pss 78](https://ref.ly/Ps78:1-Ps78:72), [106](https://ref.ly/Ps106:1-Ps106:48). • Persistent disobedience and unbelief grieved his Holy Spirit ([Ps 106:33](https://ref.ly/Ps106:33); [Matt 12:32](https://ref.ly/Matt12:32); [Mark 3:29](https://ref.ly/Mark3:29)). • he became their enemy: Examples include Israel’s period of wandering in the wilderness (see the book of Numbers), the period of the judges (see the book of Judges), and the period leading up to the Exile (see the book of Jeremiah).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:10

## Isaiah 63:14 (id: 16666)

God gave his people rest after he brought them into the Promised Land (see [63:9](https://ref.ly/Isa63:9); [Josh 1:13](https://ref.ly/Josh1:13); [22:4](https://ref.ly/Josh22:4); [23:1](https://ref.ly/Josh23:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:14

## Isaiah 63:15–64.12 (id: 16667)

The prophet’s reflections on the past ([63:7–14](https://ref.ly/Isa63:7-Isa63:14)) inspire him to pray that God would now rescue his people as he has done before.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:15–ISA 64:12

## Isaiah 63:16 (id: 16668)

our Father: God’s fatherhood and his commitment to his children are much more important and secure than national ancestry (see [9:6](https://ref.ly/Isa9:6); [64:8](https://ref.ly/Isa64:8); [Deut 32:6](https://ref.ly/Deut32:6); [Ps 68:5](https://ref.ly/Ps68:5); [Mal 2:10](https://ref.ly/Mal2:10); [Matt 6:9–15](https://ref.ly/Matt6:9-Matt6:15); [Rom 8:15–17](https://ref.ly/Rom8:15-Rom8:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:16

## Isaiah 63:17 (id: 16669)

The prophet understands that God has the power to keep his people faithful, so he asks, why have you allowed us to turn from your path? • Return and help us: God likewise has the power to call his people back to himself ([Ezek 36:25–27](https://ref.ly/Ezek36:25-Ezek36:27)) and to defeat all their enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:17

## Isaiah 63:18 (id: 16670)

The people were supposed to be holy*,* but their lack of holiness had led to destruction. • The holy place was the Temple, which the Babylonians destroyed in 586 BC ([64:11](https://ref.ly/Isa64:11); [2 Kgs 25:1–21](https://ref.ly/2Kgs25:1-2Kgs25:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:18

## Isaiah 63:19 (id: 16671)

Israel was constantly turning from God and then being punished by him.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 63:19

## Isaiah 64:5–6 (id: 16681)

constant sinners . . . infected and impure with sin: See also [59:1–15](https://ref.ly/Isa59:1-Isa59:15). The only hope for salvation and transformation is through Jesus Christ (see [Rom 7:25–8:11](https://ref.ly/Rom7:25-Rom8:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 64:5–ISA 64:6

## Isaiah 64:7 (id: 16682)

you have turned away from us: See [1:15](https://ref.ly/Isa1:15); [30:20](https://ref.ly/Isa30:20); [59:2](https://ref.ly/Isa59:2). • turned us over to our sins*:* Because the people were so bent on sinning, God left them to perish in their sinful ways (see [Rom 1:24](https://ref.ly/Rom1:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 64:7

## Isaiah 64:8 (id: 16683)

clay . . . potter: See also [29:16](https://ref.ly/Isa29:16); [45:9](https://ref.ly/Isa45:9); [Rom 9:20–21](https://ref.ly/Rom9:20-Rom9:21).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 64:8

## Isaiah 64:10 (id: 16680)

holy cities: All the cities of Judah were considered holy to God. However, the Temple in the host city of Jerusalem was the most holy place.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 64:10

## Isaiah 65:1–2 (id: 16684)

The Lord opened up every opportunity for the people of Israel to seek him ([55:6](https://ref.ly/Isa55:6); [58:2](https://ref.ly/Isa58:2)), but they did not do so.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:1–ISA 65:2

## Isaiah 65:1–66.24 (id: 16685)

Here the Lord responds to the prayer in [63:7–64:12](https://ref.ly/Isa63:7-Isa64:12).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:1–ISA 66:24

## Isaiah 65:3 (id: 16696)

Sacred gardens were a part of the fertility religion of Baal.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:3

## Isaiah 65:4 (id: 16697)

worshiping the dead: God had banned the practice of necromancy (consulting dead spirits; see [8:19–22](https://ref.ly/Isa8:19-Isa8:22); [47:9](https://ref.ly/Isa47:9); [Deut 18:9–11](https://ref.ly/Deut18:9-Deut18:11)). • the flesh of pigs . . . other forbidden foods: See [Isa 66:3–4](https://ref.ly/Isa66:3-Isa66:4); [Lev 11:7](https://ref.ly/Lev11:7); [Deut 14:3](https://ref.ly/Deut14:3), [8](https://ref.ly/Deut14:8).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:4

## Isaiah 65:5 (id: 16698)

you will defile me! I am holier than you! The people of Israel used the language of ritual purification, as stated in the laws of Moses, yet they practiced rites influenced by paganism. Because of this hypocrisy, they were a stench in God’s nostrils (see[1:10–15](https://ref.ly/Isa1:10-Isa1:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:5

## Isaiah 65:6 (id: 16699)

my decree is written out: God is fully committed to carry out his plan. • The godly had asked whether the Lord would stand silent forever ([64:12](https://ref.ly/Isa64:12)). God answered that he would not but would deal with the wicked before restoring the righteous remnant.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:6

## Isaiah 65:7 (id: 16700)

The people of Israel practiced their pagan religion at sacred shrines on mountains and hills (see [1 Kgs 14:23](https://ref.ly/1Kgs14:23); [Hos 4:13](https://ref.ly/Hos4:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:7

## Isaiah 65:8–16 (id: 16701)

The Lord planned to spare and reward a remnant of righteous people.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:8–ISA 65:16

## Isaiah 65:10 (id: 16686)

Sharon was a fertile and beautiful marshy region southwest of Mount Carmel (see [33:9](https://ref.ly/Isa33:9)). The valley of Achor in the vicinity of Jericho was associated with the curse on Achan ([Josh 7:24–26](https://ref.ly/Josh7:24-Josh7:26)); it would be transformed into a place of blessing ([Hos 2:15](https://ref.ly/Hos2:15)). These western and eastern regions might represent the renewal of the whole land.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:10

## Isaiah 65:11 (id: 16687)

Fate and Destiny are names of pagan gods (*Gad, Meni*) that were thought to bring fortune and determine one’s destiny.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:11

## Isaiah 65:12 (id: 16688)

‘destine’: This verb (Hebrew manithi) is a wordplay on Meni (see study note on 65:11). God alone controls human and national destinies.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:12
* **Associated Articles:** Isaiah 65:11 (ID: `16687@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Isaiah 65:13–15 (id: 16689)

The contrast between the wicked (addressed as you) and God’s servants pertains to all areas of life. God punishes the wicked but blesses those who truly serve him (see [65:17–25](https://ref.ly/Isa65:17-Isa65:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:13–ISA 65:15

## Isaiah 65:15 (id: 16690)

The new name given to the faithful represents a new identity and a deeper relationship with the Lord (see also [62:2](https://ref.ly/Isa62:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:15

## Isaiah 65:16 (id: 16691)

evil of earlier days: Cp. [Rev 21:4](https://ref.ly/Rev21:4).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:16

## Isaiah 65:17 (id: 16692)

The new heavens and new earth will be a place of righteousness (see also [2 Pet 3:13](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:13); [Rev 21](https://ref.ly/Rev21:1-Rev21:27)). Paul described those who believe in Christ as already being part of the new creation (see [2 Cor 5:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:17); [Gal 6:15](https://ref.ly/Gal6:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:17

## Isaiah 65:18–19 (id: 16693)

Jerusalem here symbolizes God’s eternal kingdom ([Rev 21:1–4](https://ref.ly/Rev21:1-Rev21:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:18–ISA 65:19

## Isaiah 65:24 (id: 16694)

God will be present with his people (see also [19:22](https://ref.ly/Isa19:22); [30:19](https://ref.ly/Isa30:19); cp. [1:15](https://ref.ly/Isa1:15); [59:2](https://ref.ly/Isa59:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:24

## Isaiah 65:25 (id: 16695)

The snakes represent evil ([27:1](https://ref.ly/Isa27:1); [Gen 3](https://ref.ly/Gen3:1-Gen3:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 65:25

## Isaiah 66:1 (id: 16709)

my throne . . . my footstool: God’s kingdom extends over all creation (see [40:22](https://ref.ly/Isa40:22); [Matt 5:34–35](https://ref.ly/Matt5:34-Matt5:35)). • a temple . . . a resting place: Because the entire universe is God’s dwelling place, humans cannot limit him to a building (see [1 Kgs 8:27](https://ref.ly/1Kgs8:27)). • Stephen quoted [Isa 66:1–2a](https://ref.ly/Isa66:1-Isa66:2) in his last sermon ([Acts 7:49–50](https://ref.ly/Acts7:49-Acts7:50)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:1

## Isaiah 66:2 (id: 16713)

God is pleased to dwell with those who have humble and contrite hearts ([57:15](https://ref.ly/Isa57:15); [Ps 51:17](https://ref.ly/Ps51:17)). • who tremble at my word: The humble and contrite submit themselves to God’s will, whereas the arrogant resist it.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:2

## Isaiah 66:3 (id: 16714)

delighting in their detestable sins: Literally *delighting in* *abominations,* which refers to pagan worship practices. • sacrifice a bull . . . blessed an idol: Wicked people brought sacrifices as prescribed by the law, but their sin rendered those sacrifices equivalent to pagan offerings (see [1:11–17](https://ref.ly/Isa1:11-Isa1:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:3

## Isaiah 66:6 (id: 16715)

terrible noise from the Temple: This parallels the situation described in [Ezek 9](https://ref.ly/Ezek9:1-Ezek9:11) when God’s executioner began to destroy the wicked people of Jerusalem. • vengeance against his enemies: God would deal out retribution to the disobedient members of his own people. They were his enemies because of their persistent sin and rejection of God.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:6

## Isaiah 66:7 (id: 16716)

birth pains . . . gives birth to a son: See [9:6–7](https://ref.ly/Isa9:6-Isa9:7); [54:1–3](https://ref.ly/Isa54:1-Isa54:3).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:7

## Isaiah 66:8 (id: 16717)

by the time . . . her children will be born: A miraculous repopulation of Zion would occur (see [49:19–20](https://ref.ly/Isa49:19-Isa49:20); [54:1–3](https://ref.ly/Isa54:1-Isa54:3); cp. [1:8–9](https://ref.ly/Isa1:8-Isa1:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:8

## Isaiah 66:9 (id: 16718)

The Lord promised that he would surely recreate his holy nation.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:9

## Isaiah 66:12 (id: 16702)

a river: The people, who lost peace and prosperity in the Exile, would receive it back abundantly (see [48:18](https://ref.ly/Isa48:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:12

## Isaiah 66:13 (id: 16703)

I will comfort you: Cp. [40:1](https://ref.ly/Isa40:1).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:13

## Isaiah 66:14 (id: 16704)

flourish like the grass: Contrast [40:7](https://ref.ly/Isa40:7); [64:6](https://ref.ly/Isa64:6). • God’s enemies included the disobedient from the foreign nations and from within Israel (see [61:2](https://ref.ly/Isa61:2); [66:6](https://ref.ly/Isa66:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:14

## Isaiah 66:15–16 (id: 16705)

the Lord is coming with fire: God will appear with furious judgment against his enemies (see [Ps 7:13](https://ref.ly/Ps7:13)). By contrast, he will reveal his glory to his people (see [Isa 40:5](https://ref.ly/Isa40:5), [10](https://ref.ly/Isa40:10)). • God will judge all creation as a part of the process of renewing the earth (see [24:1–4](https://ref.ly/Isa24:1-Isa24:4); [65:17](https://ref.ly/Isa65:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:15–ISA 66:16

## Isaiah 66:17 (id: 16706)

Apostates who ‘consecrate’ and ‘purify’ themselves through idolatrous practices are an abomination to God (cp.[1:28–31](https://ref.ly/Isa1:28-Isa1:31); [65:4](https://ref.ly/Isa65:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:17

## Isaiah 66:18–23 (id: 16707)

When God reveals his glory to all people, the nations join in God’s plan of redemption; they can even serve as priests and Levites before him. The godly from all nations last from generation to generation as they serve the living God.

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:18–ISA 66:23

## Isaiah 66:19 (id: 16708)

The sign is the proclamation of God’s glory among the nations ([66:20](https://ref.ly/Isa66:20)). God will establish a righteous and faithful new people consisting of godly Gentiles together with faithful Israelites ([Rev 15:3–4](https://ref.ly/Rev15:3-Rev15:4); see also [Acts 2](https://ref.ly/Acts2:1-Acts2:47)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:19

## Isaiah 66:21 (id: 16710)

That some of the Gentiles would serve as priests and Levites signifies the removal of God’s distinction between Hebrews and Gentiles (see [56:7](https://ref.ly/Isa56:7); see also [Gal 6:15](https://ref.ly/Gal6:15); [Eph 4:11–13](https://ref.ly/Eph4:11-Eph4:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:21

## Isaiah 66:22 (id: 16711)

always be my people: God’s promise to Abraham was secure ([Gen 17:7](https://ref.ly/Gen17:7); see also [Gal 3:8](https://ref.ly/Gal3:8), [14](https://ref.ly/Gal3:14)). • a name that will never disappear: The identity of this new people will last forever (see [Isa 59:21](https://ref.ly/Isa59:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:22

## Isaiah 66:24 (id: 16712)

Isaiah gives a final warning of the severity of God’s judgment. The book begins and ends with the condemnation of those who have rebelled (see [1:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa1:2-Isa1:4)). • The judgment of God on wicked humans will generate utter horror because such people will have no hope and no relief from suffering (see also [Matt 5:22](https://ref.ly/Matt5:22); [25:41](https://ref.ly/Matt25:41); [Mark 9:47–48](https://ref.ly/Mark9:47-Mark9:48); [Rev 20:11–15](https://ref.ly/Rev20:11-Rev20:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** ISA 66:24
